# LoCoBench-Agent Task

## Task Information

**Task ID**: rust_data_streaming_expert_013_architectural_understanding_expert_01
**Category**: architectural_understanding
**Difficulty**: expert
**Language**: rust
**Context Length**: 1023423 tokens
**Files**: 82

## Task Title

Architectural Refactoring for High-Velocity Ingestion in ChirpPulse

## Description

ChirpPulse is a high-performance, real-time data pipeline written in Rust. It ingests data from various social media sources, performs sentiment analysis, and stores the enriched data in a distributed data lake. The system is designed for parallelism and resilience, featuring components for stream processing, data quality checks, and monitoring. The engineering team is preparing to integrate a new, extremely high-throughput 'FireHose' data source. There is a significant concern that the current architecture, specifically the sentiment analysis stage, will become a bottleneck under the new load, leading to backpressure that could stall the entire ingestion pipeline or cause data loss.

## Your Task

Your task is to analyze the ChirpPulse architecture and propose a modification to handle the anticipated increase in data volume. You must not write any code, but provide a detailed architectural assessment and plan.

1.  **Map the Pipeline:** Identify the primary stages of the data processing pipeline from ingestion to final storage. For each stage, identify the key module(s) responsible for its logic.
2.  **Identify the Bottleneck Coupling:** Pinpoint the specific mechanism used to hand off data between the data normalization/transformation stage and the sentiment analysis stage. Describe how this mechanism could cause the backpressure problem.
3.  **Propose an Architectural Solution:** Design a modification to the architecture that decouples the sentiment analysis stage from the main ingestion pipeline, allowing it to scale independently and absorb massive load variations. Your proposal should be a well-established architectural pattern.
4.  **Justify Your Solution:** Explain why your proposed architecture is superior for this use case. Discuss its impact on scalability, system resilience, and backpressure handling.
5.  **Identify Affected Components:** List the specific modules that would need to be modified to implement your proposed solution and briefly describe the nature of the changes required for each.

## Expected Approach

An expert developer would approach this by first trying to get a high-level overview of the system without diving into every file. 

1.  **Initial Reconnaissance:** The developer would start by examining `config.txt` to understand the system's configurable parts (e.g., worker pool sizes, queue depths, endpoint URLs, feature flags). They would also look at `package.json` to identify key dependencies like `tokio`, `rayon`, `serde`, and potentially a message queue client or an NLP library, which give strong hints about the system's nature.
2.  **Trace the Data Flow:** The developer would then try to find the main orchestration logic, likely in a large, central module (e.g., `module_22.txt` or `module_79.txt`). From there, they would trace the flow of data. This involves identifying the primary data structures (e.g., `RawEvent`, `NormalizedChirp`, `EnrichedSentimentData`) and following them through function calls and channel senders/receivers across different modules.
3.  **Identify Key Modules:** By tracing the data, they would associate functionality with the obfuscated module names. For example, the module that deserializes raw JSON into a struct is likely part of ingestion. The module that performs complex string operations and validation is transformation. The module that contains a loop calling a CPU-intensive function is likely the sentiment analysis core. The module using an AWS S3 SDK is the storage sink.
4.  **Analyze Inter-Component Communication:** The developer would pay close attention to how these identified components communicate. They would recognize the use of `tokio::mpsc::channel` as a common pattern for in-process, asynchronous communication. Upon finding the channel between the normalization and sentiment analysis stages, they would immediately identify it as a point of tight coupling and a potential source of backpressure if the consumer (sentiment analysis) is slower than the producer (normalization).
5.  **Formulate a Solution:** Recognizing the tight coupling/bottleneck issue, the expert would apply a standard distributed systems pattern: introducing a message broker/queue. This decouples the producer and consumer, provides a durable buffer, and allows the two services to be scaled independently. They would then map this abstract pattern back to the specific codebase, identifying which modules need to become producers and which need to become consumers.

## Evaluation Criteria

- **Pipeline Identification (20%):** Correctly identifies the 3-4 primary stages of the pipeline and maps them to the correct modules.
- **Bottleneck Analysis (25%):** Accurately identifies the `tokio::mpsc::channel` as the coupling mechanism and correctly explains how it causes backpressure in this context.
- **Solution Quality (25%):** Proposes a robust, industry-standard decoupling solution, such as using an external message queue.
- **Architectural Justification (15%):** Clearly articulates the benefits of the proposed solution in terms of scalability, resilience, and backpressure handling.
- **Impact Assessment (15%):** Correctly identifies all the key modules (`normalization`, `sentiment`, `orchestration`, `config`) that require modification to implement the proposed change.

57-assistanttool_useRead
58-usertool_resultRead
     1→```rust
     2→//! src/constants.rs
     3→//!
     4→//! A centralized place for compile-time and runtime configuration constants
     5→//! that are shared across ChirpPulse crates and binaries.  Keeping constants
     6→//! here encourages re-use, prevents magic numbers/strings from leaking into
     7→//! business logic, and makes it easier to discover tunables that may need to
     8→//! be surfaced as configuration knobs in the future.
     9→//!
    10→//! Most values are compile-time constants (`const` or `static`).  When a
    11→//! setting must be fetched from the environment at runtime we wrap it in
    12→//! a `once_cell::sync::Lazy` to incur exactly one `std::env::var()` call
    13→//! across the entire process lifetime.
    14→//!
    15→//! NOTE: Although this file is placed under `src/constants.txt` by request,
    16→//! Cargo will only compile `*.rs` files.  Rename to `constants.rs` or include
    17→//! via `include_str!` if you intend to embed the file verbatim.
    18→
    19→use std::time::Duration;
    20→use std::num::NonZeroUsize;
    21→use once_cell::sync::Lazy;
    22→
    23→/// Human-readable service identifier used in logs, tracing spans, and metrics.
    24→pub const SERVICE_NAME: &str = "ChirpPulse";
    25→
    26→/// Current semver of this crate.  Keep in sync with `Cargo.toml`.
    27→pub const VERSION: &str = env!("CARGO_PKG_VERSION");
    28→

98-assistanttext-
I have completed the architectural analysis of ChirpPulse. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Analysis Complete

### 1. Pipeline Mapping (4 Primary Stages)
- **Ingestion**: Consumes raw events from social sources via Kafka (modules 12, 47, 70)
- **Normalization/QC**: Schema validation, deduplication, PII removal (modules 79, 29, 41)
- **Sentiment Analysis/Enrichment**: CPU-intensive scoring and toxicity detection (modules 22, 27, 56)
- **Storage Sink**: Writes to Apache Iceberg via Kafka (module 65)

### 2. Bottleneck Identified
The critical coupling is in **module_27.txt** at lines 216-217:
```rust
const CHANNEL_DEPTH: usize = 1_024;
let (in_tx, in_rx) = mpsc::channel(CHANNEL_DEPTH);
let (out_tx, out_rx) = mpsc::channel(CHANNEL_DEPTH);
```

This bounded `tokio::sync::mpsc` channel creates tight coupling between normalization and sentiment analysis. When the sentiment stage (slow consumer) can't keep pace, the 1,024-event buffer fills, blocking the producer and propagating backpressure upstream.

### 3. Proposed Solution: Message Queue Decoupling
Replace the in-process mpsc channel with an external **Apache Kafka topic** (`chirp.normalized.events`) to decouple the stages. This enables:
- Independent horizontal scaling of sentiment consumers
- Durable buffering during load spikes
- Elastic backpressure absorption
- Fault tolerance

### 4. Affected Modules
- **module_27**: Replace mpsc with Kafka producer
- **module_22**: Update to consume from new intermediate topic
- **module_56**: Replace mpsc receiver with Kafka consumer
- **config.txt**: Add new pipeline configuration
- **constants.txt**: Add new topic constant

The complete solution with code evidence and detailed implementation guidance has been written to `/logs/agent/solution.md`.

                                                       |\n|----------------------------|-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|\n| Stream Processing          | Zero-copy ingestion, back-pressure control, dynamic topic routing, _exactly-once_ semantics via **Kafka** |\n| Enrichment & ETL           | Strategy-pattern plug-ins (language detection, toxicity scoring, graph extraction, location resolution)    |\n| Storage & Lakehouse        | **Apache Iceberg** tables (schema evolution, partition pruning, ACID)                                      |\n| Query & Analytics          | Real-time aggregations with **Materialize** connectors; batch OLAP via **DuckDB**                          |\n| Observability & Resilience | Self-healing consumer groups, end-to-end tracing (OpenTelemetry), circuit-breaker patterns                 |\n| Deployment                 | Kubernetes Helm charts, `docker-compose` sandbox, GitHub Actions CI/CD                                     |\n\n---\n\n## \ud83c\udfd7\ufe0f Architecture Overview\n\n```mermaid\ngraph LR\n  subgraph Ingestion\n    TW(Twitter Firehose) -->|JSON| G[Gateway Service]\n    RD(Reddit Stream) --> G\n    DC(Discord IRC) --> G\n  end\n\n  G -->|Avro/Kafka| Q[Quality Control]\n  Q -->|Kafka| E[Enrichment Workers]\n  E -->|Parquet| L[Iceberg Data Lake]\n  L -->|Materialized Views| D[(Dashboards)]\n  L -->|gRPC| API{{/api/v1}}\n```\n\n* **Gateway Service** \u2013 Authenticates providers, normalizes payloads, and writes events to Kafka topics.<br>\n* **Quality Control** \u2013 Deduplicates, validates schema, and enforces PII removal.<br>\n* **Enrichment Workers** \u2013 _Hot-swappable_ algorithms, loaded via the Strategy pattern.<br>\n* **Data Lake** \u2013 Iceberg tables stored on S3/GCS; versioned with snapshots.<br>\n* **Dashboards & API** \u2013 Serve insights to humans and automated agents.\n\n---\n\n## \ud83d\ude80 Quick Start (Local Sandbox)\n\n> Requirements: `docker`, Layout\n\n```\nchirppulse/\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 crates/\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 chirppulse-common/      # Models, error types, telemetry\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 chirppulse-ingest/      # strategy::{EnrichmentError, EnrichmentStrategy},\n};\n\n/// A toy sentiment analyzer that counts positive words.\npub struct SimpleSentiment;\n\n#[async_trait]\nimpl EnrichmentStrategy for SimpleSentiment {\n    async fn enrich(&self, ev: Event) -> Result<EnrichedEvent, EnrichmentError> {\n        let positives = [\"great\", \"awesome\", \"\ud83c\udf89\", \"\ud83d\ude80\"];\n        let score = ev\n            .body\n            .split_whitespace()\n            .filter(|word| positives.contains(word))\n            .count() as f32;\n\n        Ok(EnrichedEvent {\n            metadata: ev.metadata,\n            body: ev.body,\n            sentiment_score: score,\n            ..Default::default()\n        })\n    }\n\n    fn name(&self) -> &'static str {\n        \"simple_sentiment\"\n    }\n}\n```\n\nRegister the strategy at runtime:\n\n```rust\n// in enrich/src/main.rs\nuse chirppulse_enrich::Pipeline;\n\n#[tokio::main]\nasync fn main() -> anyhow::Result<()> {\n    let mut pipeline = Pipeline::new().await?;\n    pipeline.register(Box::new(SimpleSentiment));\n    pipeline.run().await\n}\n```\n\nThanks to dynamic reloading, new strategies can be hot-swapped Connect to the real-time event fire-hose.  \n2. Configure an enrichment pipeline.  \n3. Publish analytic results back to Kafka / Iceberg.  \n4. Extend the platform with a **custom strategy** (plug-in) that can be hot-swapped in production.\n\n---\n\n## Quick-Start\n\nAdd the SDK to your `Cargo.toml`:\n\n```toml\n[dependencies]\nchirp-pulse = { version = \"0.9\", features = [\"streams\", \"strategy\"] }\ntokio        = { version = \"1\",   features = [\"full\"] }\n```\n\nConsumers are fully `async` and integrate with the Tokio runtime.\n\n---\n\n## Data Model\n\n```rust\nuse chrono::{DateTime, Utc};\nuse serde::{Deserialize, Serialize};\nuse uuid::Uuid;\n\n/// A flattened representation of any micro-interaction captured by ChirpPulse.\n///\n/// The schema is forward-compatible and will evolve with optional fields.\n/// Unknown fields must be gracefully ignored by downstream services.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct SocialEvent {\n    /// Unique, idempotent identifier applied by the ingestion layer.\n    pub id: Uuid,\n\n    /// Original platform: twitter, reddit, mastodon, etc.\n    pub source: &'static str,\n\n    /// RFC-3339 timestamp of when the event was GENERATED on its native platform.\n    pub occurred_at: DateTime<Utc>,\n\n    /// The raw, unmodified payload\n    pub payload: serde_json::Value,\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Streaming the Fire-Hose\n\n```rust,no_run\nuse chirp_pulse::sdk::{\n    firehose::{FireHoseConsumer, FireHoseConfig},\n    prelude::*,\n};\nuse tokio_stream::StreamExt;\n\n#[tokio::main]\nasync fn main() -> Result<(), chirp_pulse::Error> {\n    // 1. Create a config with sensible defaults + overrides.\n    let cfg = FireHoseConfig::builder()\n        .brokers([\"kafka-broker-1:9092\", \"kafka-broker-2:9092\"])\n        .group_id(\"brand-insights-team\")\n        .topic(\"chirppulse.firehose.raw\")\n        .auto_commit_interval_ms(5_000)\n        .build()?;\n\n    // 2. Stand-up an asynchronous consumer.\n    let mut consumer = FireHoseConsumer::connect(cfg).await?;\n\n    // 3. Consume indefinitely, applying back-pressure automatically.\n    while let Some(event) = consumer.next().await {\n        match event {\n            Ok(record) => {\n                println!(\n                    \"Got event {} from {} at {}\",\n                    record.value.id, record.value.source, record.value.occurred_at\n                );\n            }\n            Err(e) => {\n                // Non-fatal parsing errors (e.g. schema evolution) can be logged & skipped.\n                eprintln!(\"\u26a0\ufe0f  Undeserializable record skipped: {e:?}\");\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    Ok(())\n}\n```\n\nKey characteristics:\n* **At-least-once** delivery with idempotent IDs.\n* **Offset management** handled by the SDK (exposed for advanced use-cases).\n* Transparent **schema evolution** support via Serde\u2019s non-strict deserialization.\n\n---\n\n## Enrichment Pipelines\n\nChirpPulse ships with an opinionated but extensible ETL pipeline expressed as an\n**observer pattern** backed by **Kafka Streams**.  \nBelow is a complete, runnable example that adds *language detection* and a custom\n*toxicity score* while enforcing data-quality thresholds.\n\n```rust,no_run\nuse chirp_pulse::{\n    sdk::{\n        enrich::{Pipeline, Stage},\n        firehose::{FireHoseConsumer, FireHoseConfig},\n        producers::TopicProducer,\n    },\n    algorithms::{language::LangDetector, toxicity::ToxicityClassifier},\n};\n\n#[tokio::main]\nasync fn main() -> Result<(), chirp_pulse::Error> {\n    // Build ingestion side.\n    let source_cfg = FireHoseConfig::builder()\n        .topic(\"chirppulse.firehose.raw\")\n        .group_id(\"enrichment-worker-a\")\n        .build()?;\n    let mut firehose = FireHoseConsumer::connect(source_cfg).await?;\n\n    // Build egress side.\n    let sink = TopicProducer::builder()\n        .topic(\"chirppulse.firehose.enriched\")\n        .brokers([\"kafka-broker-1:9092\"])\n        .build()?;\n\n    // Compose the pipeline.\n    let pipeline = Pipeline::new()\n        .with_stage(Stage::sync(\"language\", LangDetector::default()))\n        .with_stage(Stage::async(\"toxicity\", ToxicityClassifier::new(0.85)?))\n        .with_stage(Stage::sync(\"qc\", |mut event| {\n            // Drop events that don't meet minimum quality scores.\n            if let Some(tox) = event\n                .metadata\n                .get(\"toxicity\")\n                .and_then(|v| v.as_f64())\n            {\n                if tox > 0.95 {\n                    // Reject extreme toxicity\n                    return None;\n                }\n            }\n            Some(event)\n        }));\n\n    // Run forever \u2014 pipeline maintains back-pressure internally.\n    while let Some(event) = firehose.next().await.transpose()? {\n        if let Some(enriched) = pipeline.process(event).await? {\n            sink.send(&enriched).await?;\n        }\n    }\n\n    Ok(())\n}\n```\n\n### Building Blocks\n\n* `Stage::sync` \u2013 executes on the current task; suited for CPU-bound, fast ops.  \n* `Stage::async` \u2013 spawns a bounded task-pool; suited for I/O or heavy compute.  \n* `Pipeline::process` \u2013 short-circuit returns `None` to **filter** events.\n\n---\n\n## Implementing a Custom Strategy\n\nAnalytical algorithms are loaded via an SPI-like **Strategy pattern** allowing them\nto be upgraded *without cluster downtime*.\n\n```rust,no_run\nuse async_trait::async_trait;\nuse chirp_pulse::sdk::strategy::{AnalysisCtx, Strategy};\n\n/// Counts emoji usage in real-time.\npub struct EmojiRadar;\n\n#[async_trait]\nimpl Strategy for EmojiRadar {\n    const NAME: &'static str = \"emoji-radar\";\n    type Error = anyhow::Error;\n\n    async fn analyze(&self, ctx: &AnalysisCtx) -> Result<(), Self::Error> {\n        let event = &ctx.event;\n\n        let text = event\n            .payload\n            .get(\"text\")\n            .and_then(|v| v.as_str())\n            .unwrap_or_default();\n\n        let emoji_count = text.chars().filter(|c| c.is_emoji_presentation()).count();\n\n        ctx.emit_metric(\"emoji_count\", emoji_count as f64).await?;\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n```\n\nTo register your strategy at runtime:\n\n```rust\nuse chirp_pulse::sdk::strategy::{StrategyLoader, StrategyServer};\n\n#[tokio::main]\nasync fn main() -> Result<(), chirp_pulse::Error> {\n    StrategyLoader::default()\n        .register(Box::new(EmojiRadar))\n        .load()?;\n\n    StrategyServer::bind(\"0.0.0.0:8080\").await?.run_forever().await\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## REST / gRPC Gateways\n\nEvery microservice exposes **OpenAPI v3** & **gRPC** reflection at `/api`.\nExample (TypeScript generated client shown for completeness):\n\n```rust,ignore\n// Equivalent Rust client is autogenerated via `tonic-build`.\nimport {FireHoseClient} from 'chirp-pulse/clients/firehose';\n\nconst client = new FireHoseClient('grpc+tls://firehose.chirppulse.io');\n\nconst stream = client.tail({topic: 'chirppulse.firehose.enriched'});\n\nfor await (const event of stream) {\n  console.log(event.id, event.source);\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Back-Pressure & Retry Semantics\n\nAll producers and consumers expose a `pending()` gauge and `flush()` async call\nallowing you to gracefully drain in-flight messages before shutdown signals.\n\n```rust,no_run\nsignal_hook::flag::register_conditional_default(\n    signal_hook::consts::SIGTERM,\n    || {\n        println!(\"Shutdown requested. Flushing\u2026\");\n        producer.flush(); // async barrier\n    },\n);\n```\n\n---\n\n## Error Handling\n\n* **Typed errors** (`chirp_pulse::Error`) cover connection failures, schema problems,\n  and pipeline time-outs.\n* Every fatal error is reported to **OpenTelemetry** traces *and* bubbled up.\n\n```rust\nmatch consumer.next().await {\n    Some(Err(chirp_pulse::Error::Deserializer(e))) => {\n        metrics::increment_counter!(\"events_deser_failed\");\n        // The SDK automatically commits the offset to avoid poison-pill loops.\n    }\n    Some(Err(e)) => return Err(e.into()),\n    Some(Ok(event)) => { /* happy path */ }\n    None => unreachable!(\"stream never ends\"),\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Contributing\n\nPull-requests must pass:\n\n1. `cargo fmt --all -- --check`  \n2. `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`  \n3. `cargo test` \u2013 including integration tests that target a **real** Kafka test-container.\n\n---\n\n\u00a9 2023\u2013present **ChirpPulse**.  \nLicensed under Apache-2.0.\n```",

rules.iter() {\n            // For every rule we catch its error separately to emit per-rule metrics.\n            match rule.check(event).await {\n                Ok(()) => increment_counter!(\"rule_pass_total\", \"rule\" => rule.name()),\n                Err(err) => {\n                    increment_counter!(\"rule_fail_total\", \"rule\" => rule.name());\n     "content": "```rust\n//! module_22 \u2013 Runtime-hot-swappable sentiment analysis strategies and Kafka\n//! stream processor used by ChirpPulse.\n//!\n//! This module demonstrates how data-scientists can plug-in new sentiment\n//! algorithms without taking the pipeline offline.  A registry keeps multiple\n//! strategies in memory and a lightweight control message on the\n//! `STRATEGY_CONTROL_TOPIC` lets operators promote a new default strategy\n//! instantly.  The processor consumes raw social messages, enriches them with\n//! sentiment, and republishes them to the lake in real-time.\n//!\n//! Production-ready aspects demonstrated here:\n//! \u2022 async Kafka consumer/producer (`rdkafka` + `tokio`)  \n//! \u2022 Strategy pattern with dynamic dispatch & hot-swap capabilities  \n//! \u2022 Robust error handling (`thiserror`) and observability (`tracing`)  \n//! \u2022 Graceful back-pressure and DLQ for poison messages  \n//!\n//! NOTE: In a real deployment this module would live in its own crate with the\n//! dependencies declared in `Cargo.toml`.  For brevity all source is presented\n//! in a single file.\n\nuse std::{\n    collections::HashMap,\n    sync::Arc,\n    time::{Duration, SystemTime},\n};\n\nuse async_trait::async_trait;\nuse futures::{future::Either, StreamExt};\nuse rdkafka::{\n    consumer::{Consumer, StreamConsumer},\n    error::KafkaError,\n    message::{BorrowedMessage, OwnedMessage},\n    producer::{FutureProducer, FutureRecord},\n    ClientConfig, Message,\n};\nuse serde::{Deserialize, Serialize};\nuse thiserror::Error;\nuse tokio::sync::{mpsc, RwLock};\nuse tracing::{debug, error, info, warn};\n\n///////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////\n// Domain models\n///////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////\n\n/// An enriched sentiment score produced by an analysis algorithm.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct SentimentScore {\n    /// Final sentiment in `[-1.0, 1.0]` where -1 is negative, 1 positive.\n    pub polarity: f32,\n    /// Confidence score in `[0, 1]`.\n    pub confidence: f32,\n    /// Optional explanation payload which some advanced models emit.\n    pub meta: Option<serde_json::Value>,\n}\n\n/// The wire format for an input social message ingested from Kafka.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct SocialMessage {\n    pub id: String,\n    pub user_id: String,\n    pub platform: String,\n    pub language: String,\n    pub text: String,\n    pub created_at: SystemTime,\n}\n\n/// Combined structure sent to the downstream lake after enrichment.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct EnrichedSocialMessage {\n    #[serde(flatten)]\n    pub original: SocialMessage,\n    pub sentiment: SentimentScore,\n    /// The algorithm identifier that produced the score.\n    pub strategy: String,\n    /// Event time for the enrichment.\n    pub enriched_at: SystemTime,\n}\n\n///////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////\n// Errors\n///////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////\n\n#[derive(Debug, Error)]\npub enum ProcessorError {\n    #[error(\"kafka error: {0}\")]\n    Kafka(#[from] KafkaError),\n    #[error(\"strategy '{0}' not found\")]\n    StrategyNotFound(String),\n    #[error(\"json serialization error: {0}\")]\n    Json(#[from] serde_json::Error),\n    #[error(\"channel error: {0}\")]\n    Channel(#[from] mpsc::error::SendError<OwnedMessage>),\n    #[error(\"other: {0}\")]\n    Other(String),\n}\n\n///////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////\n// Sentiment Strategy Pattern\n///////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////\n\n/// Trait representing any sentiment analysis algorithm.\n///\n/// The `analyze` function is async to allow network calls (e.g., model server).\n#[async_trait]\npub trait SentimentStrategy: Send + Sync + 'static {\n    /// Identifier shown in telemetry and persisted to records.\n    fn name(&self) -> &'static str;\n\n    /// Perform sentiment analysis on the given message body.\n    async fn analyze(&self, text: &str) -> Result<SentimentScore, ProcessorError>;\n}\n\n/// Trivial implementation that returns neutral sentiment.\n/// Useful as a circuit-breaker fallback.\npub struct NeutralStrategy;\n\n#[async_trait]\nimpl SentimentStrategy for NeutralStrategy {\n    fn name(&self) -> &'static str {\n        \"neutral\"\n    }\n\n    async fn analyze(&self, _text: &str) -> Result<SentimentScore, ProcessorError> {\n        Ok(SentimentScore {\n            polarity: 0.0,\n            confidence: 0.0,\n            meta: None,\n        })\n    }\n}\n\n/// Example lexical strategy that looks for positive/negative keywords\n/// (purely demonstrative \u2013 not production grade).\npub struct LexiconStrategy {\n    positives: Vec<&'static str>,\n    negatives: Vec<&'static str>,\n}\n\nimpl Default for LexiconStrategy {\n    fn default() -> Self {\n        Self {\n            positives: vec![\"good\", \"great\", \"love\", \"excellent\", \"happy\"],\n            negatives: vec![\"bad\", \"hate\", \"terrible\", \"awful\", \"sad\"],\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n#[async_trait]\nimpl SentimentStrategy for LexiconStrategy {\n    fn name(&self) -> &'static str {\n        \"lexicon_v1\"\n    }\n\n    async fn analyze(&self, text: &str) -> Result<SentimentScore, ProcessorError> {\n        let mut score = 0f32;\n        let mut hits = 0u32;\n\n        for token in text.split_whitespace() {\n            if self.positives.iter().any(|p| token.eq_ignore_ascii_case(p)) {\n                score += 1.0;\n                hits += 1;\n            } else if self.negatives.iter().any(|n| token.eq_ignore_ascii_case(n)) {\n                score -= 1.0;\n                hits += 1;\n            }\n        }\n\n        if hits == 0 {\n            // Unknown sentiment\n            return Ok(SentimentScore {\n                polarity: 0.0,\n                confidence: 0.0,\n                meta: None,\n            });\n        }\n\n        let polarity = (score / hits as f32).clamp(-1.0, 1.0);\n        Ok(SentimentScore {\n            polarity,\n            confidence: (hits as f32 / text.split_whitespace().count() as f32).clamp(0.0, 1.0),\n            meta: None,\n        })\n    }\n}\n\n/// Registry containing all available strategies and the currently active default one.\n#[derive(Clone)]\npub struct StrategyRegistry {\n    strategies: Arc<RwLock<HashMap<String, Arc<dyn SentimentStrategy>>>>,\n    default: Arc<RwLock<String>>,\n}\n\nimpl StrategyRegistry {\n    pub fn new() -> Self {\n        let mut map: HashMap<String, Arc<dyn SentimentStrategy>> = HashMap::new();\n        let neutral = Arc::new(NeutralStrategy);\n        map.insert(neutral.name().to_owned(), neutral.clone());\n\n        let lex = Arc::new(LexiconStrategy::default());\n        map.insert(lex.name().to_owned(), lex.clone());\n\n        Self {\n            strategies: Arc::new(RwLock::new(map)),\n            default: Arc::new(RwLock::new(lex.name().to_owned())),\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Register or override a strategy at runtime.\n    pub async fn register<S: SentimentStrategy>(&self, strategy: S) {\n        let name = strategy.name().to_owned();\n        self.strategies\n            .write()\n            .await\n            .insert(name, Arc::new(strategy));\n    }\n\n    /// Promote the named strategy to be the default going forward.\n    pub async fn promote_default(&self, name: &str) -> Result<(), ProcessorError> {\n        let read = self.strategies.read().await;\n        if read.contains_key(name) {\n            *self.default.write().await = name.to_owned();\n            Ok(())\n        } else {\n            Err(ProcessorError::StrategyNotFound(name.to_owned()))\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Get the current default strategy.\n    pub async fn default(&self) -> Arc<dyn SentimentStrategy> {\n        let name = self.default.read().await.clone();\n        self.get(&name)\n            .await\n            .unwrap_or_else(|_| Arc::new(NeutralStrategy))\n    }\n\n    /// Fetch a strategy by name.\n    pub async fn get(&self, name: &str) -> Result<Arc<dyn SentimentStrategy>, ProcessorError> {\n        self.strategies\n            .read()\n            .await\n            .get(name)\n            .cloned()\n            .ok_or_else(|| ProcessorError::StrategyNotFound(name.into()))\n    }\n}\n\n///////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////\n// Kafka configuration helpers\n///////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////\n\nconst INPUT_TOPIC: &str = \"raw_social_stream\";\nconst OUTPUT_TOPIC: &str = \"enriched_social_stream\";\nconst DLQ_TOPIC: &str = \"enrichment_dlq\";\nconst STRATEGY_CONTROL_TOPIC: &str = \"sentiment_strategy_ctrl\";\n\nfn kafka_config(brokers: &str, group_id: &str) -> ClientConfig {\n    let mut cfg = ClientConfig::new();\n    cfg.set(\"bootstrap.servers\", brokers)\n        .set(\"enable.auto.commit\", \"false\")\n        .set(\"auto.offset.reset\", \"earliest\")\n        .set(\"group.id\", group_id)\n        .set(\"fetch.message.max.bytes\", \"1048576\") // 1 MiB\n        .set(\"message.timeout.ms\", \"5000\");\n    cfg\n}\n\nfn build_consumer(brokers: &str, group_id: &str) -> Result<StreamConsumer, KafkaError> {\n    kafka_config(brokers, group_id)\n        .create::<StreamConsumer>()\n}\n\nfn build_producer(brokers: &str) -> Result<FutureProducer, KafkaError> {\n    ClientConfig::new()\n        .set(\"bootstrap.servers\", brokers)\n        .set(\"message.timeout.ms\", \"5000\")\n        .set(\"compression.type\", \"lz4\")\n        .create::<FutureProducer>()\n}\n\n///////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////\n// Stream Processor\n///////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////\n\npub struct StreamProcessor {\n    registry: StrategyRegistry,\n    consumer: StreamConsumer,\n    producer: FutureProducer,\n}\n\nimpl StreamProcessor {\n    pub fn new(\n        registry: StrategyRegistry,\n        consumer: StreamConsumer,\n        producer: FutureProducer,\n    ) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            registry,\n            consumer,\n            producer,\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Run the event loop until process is terminated.\n    pub async fn run(mut self) -> Result<(), ProcessorError> {\n        // Subscribe to both the data topic and the control topic\n        self.consumer\n            .subscribe(&[INPUT_TOPIC, STRATEGY_CONTROL_TOPIC])?;\n\n        info!(\"Sentiment enrichment processor started, awaiting messages...\");\n        let (dlq_tx, mut dlq_rx) = mpsc::channel::<OwnedMessage>(1024);\n\n        // Spawn DLQ producer\n        let producer_clone = self.producer.clone();\n        tokio::spawn(async move {\n            while let Some(msg) = dlq_rx.recv().await {\n                let payload = msg.payload().unwrap_or_default();\n                if let Err(e) = producer_clone\n                    .send(\n                        FutureRecord::to(DLQ_TOPIC)\n                            .payload(payload)\n                            .key(msg.key().unwrap_or_default()),\n                        Duration::from_secs(0),\n                    )\n                    .await\n                {\n                    error!(\"failed to produce to DLQ: {}\", e.0);\n                }\n            }\n        });\n\n        let stream = self.consumer.stream();\n        tokio::pin!(stream);\n\n        while let Some(result) = stream.next().await {\n            match result {\n                Ok(msg) => {\n                    let topic = msg.topic().to_owned();\n                    let owned = msg.detach();\n\n                    let registry = self.registry.clone();\n                    let producer = self.producer.clone();\n                    let dlq_tx = dlq_tx.clone();\n\n                    tokio::spawn(async move {\n                        if let Err(err) =\n                            Self::handle_message(owned, &topic, registry, producer, dlq_tx).await\n                        {\n                            error!(\"processing error: {:?}\", err);\n                        }\n                    });\n                }\n                Err(e) => {\n                    warn!(\"Kafka error encountered: {}\", e);\n                }\n            }\n        }\n        Ok(())\n    }\n\n    async fn handle_message(\n        msg: OwnedMessage,\n        topic: &str,\n        registry: StrategyRegistry,\n        producer: FutureProducer,\n        dlq_tx: mpsc::Sender<OwnedMessage>,\n    ) -> Result<(), ProcessorError> {\n        match topic {\n            INPUT_TOPIC => {\n                let payload = std::str::from_utf8(msg.payload().unwrap_or_default())\n                    .map_err(|e| ProcessorError::Other(e.to_string()))?;\n\n                let social: SocialMessage = match serde_json::from_str(payload) {\n                    Ok(v) => v,\n                    Err(e) => {\n                        warn!(\"invalid JSON payload, sending to DLQ: {}\", e);\n                        dlq_tx.send(msg).await?;\n                        return Ok(());\n                    }\n                };\n\n                let strategy = registry.default().await;\n                let sentiment = strategy.analyze(&social.text).await?;\n\n                let enriched = EnrichedSocialMessage {\n                    original: social,\n                    sentiment,\n                    strategy: strategy.name().to_owned(),\n                    enriched_at: SystemTime::now(),\n                };\n\n                let serialized = serde_json::to_vec(&enriched)?;\n\n                // produce to output topic\n                producer\n                    .send(\n                        FutureRecord::to(OUTPUT_TOPIC)\n                            .payload(&serialized)\n                            .key(&enriched.original.id),\n                        Duration::from_secs(0),\n                    )\n                    .await\n                    .map_err(|(e, _)| ProcessorError::Kafka(e))?;\n\n                // manual commit\n                if let Err(e) = msg.commit(&producer.client(), rdkafka::consumer::CommitMode::Async)\n                {\n                    warn!(\"commit failed: {}\", e);\n                }\n            }\n            STRATEGY_CONTROL_TOPIC => {\n                let cmd: StrategyControl =\n                    serde_json::from_slice(msg.payload().unwrap_or_default())?;\n\n                match cmd {\n                    StrategyControl::Promote { name } => {\n                        registry.promote_default(&name).await?;\n                        info!(\"Promoted strategy '{}' as new default\", &name);\n                    }\n                }\n            }\n            _ => {\n                warn!(\"message on unexpected topic '{}', ignoring\", topic);\n            }\n        }\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n\n///////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////\n// Strategy Control Plane\n///////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////\n\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\n#[serde(tag = \"type\", rename_all = \"snake_case\")]\npub enum StrategyControl {\n    Promote { name: String },\n}\n\n///////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////\n// Embedded integration test (requires assert!(res.polarity.abs() > 0.0);\n    }\n\n    /// Registry promotion logic.\n    #[tokio::test]\n    async fn test_registry_promote() {\n        let registry = StrategyRegistry::new();\n        registry.promote_default(\"neutral\").await.unwrap();\n        let default = registry.default().await;\n        assert_eq!(default.name(), \"neutral\");\n    }\n\n    /// Ensure invalid promotion   fn test_strategy_control_ser() {\n        let msg = StrategyControl::Promote {\n            name: \"lexicon_v1\".into(),\n        };\n        let json = serde_json::to_string(&msg).unwrap();\n     "content": "// src/module_78.rs\n\n//! Real-time enrichment and quality control pipeline.\n//!\n//! This module implements a configurable, pluggable enrichment pipeline that\n//! continuously consumes `SocialEvent` items from a Kafka topic (or any\n//! compatible [`Stream`]) and publishes the transformed events to downstream\n//! sinks.  The design follows the Strategy Pattern so that new enrichment\n//! algorithms can be hot-swapped without recompiling the rest of the\n//! application.\n//\n// Features demonstrated:\n// * Parallel execution of enrichment strategies (tokio tasks / Rayon optional).\n// * Data-quality checks w/ pluggable validation rules.\n// * Scheduling of maintenance tasks (retention, compaction) using cron\n//   patterns.\n// * Observability via [`tracing`] and [`metrics`].\n// * Graceful error handling and back-pressure aware stream processing.\n\nuse std::{\n    collections::HashMap,\n    future::Future,\n    pin::Pin,\n    sync::Arc,\n    time::{Duration, SystemTime},\n};\n\nuse async_trait::async_trait;\nuse chrono::{DateTime, Utc};\nuse futures::{stream::FuturesUnordered, Stream, StreamExt};\nuse metrics::{counter, gauge, histogram};\nuse serde::{Deserialize, Serialize};\nuse tokio::{\n    select,\n    sync::mpsc::{self, Receiver, Sender},\n    task,\n    time,\n};\nuse tracing::{debug, error, info, instrument, warn};\n\n/// Maximum number of concurrent events that may be processed.\n///\n/// In practice this would be tuned according to CPU/RAM and downstream\n/// throughput characteristics.\nconst MAX_CONCURRENT_EVENTS: usize = 1024;\n\n/// A domain object representing a single unit of social data that entered the\n/// platform.\n///\n/// The struct is intentionally minimal; any number of optional metadata values\n/// may live under `tags`.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct SocialEvent {\n    pub event_id: String,\n    pub author_id: String,\n    pub created_at: DateTime<Utc>,\n    pub text: String,\n\n    /// Additional, arbitrary metadata appended by upstream sources.\n    pub tags: HashMap<String, String>,\n}\n\n/// An enriched version of [`SocialEvent`].\n///\n/// Enrichment strategies may add or mutate fields, but never remove them.  We\n/// separate the enriched event into its own type to provide compile-time\n/// guarantees that mandatory enrichment has been executed.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct EnrichedEvent {\n    pub base: SocialEvent,\n\n    /// ISO-639 language code (e.g. \"en\", \"es\").\n    pub language: Option<String>,\n\n    /// Toxicity score between 0.0 and 1.0 where 1.0 is highly toxic.\n    pub toxicity_score: Option<f32>,\n\n    /// Arbitrary extra tags.\n    pub extra: HashMap<String, String>,\n}\n\n/// Errors that can occur during enrichment or quality checks.\n#[derive(thiserror::Error, Debug)]\npub enum PipelineError {\n    #[error(\"enrichment failed: {0}\")]\n    Enrichment(#[from] anyhow::Error),\n\n    #[error(\"data quality violation: {0}\")]\n    Validation(String),\n\n    #[error(\"I/O error: {0}\")]\n    Io(#[from] std::io::Error),\n\n    #[error(\"channel closed\")]\n    ChannelClosed,\n}\n\n/// Strategy pattern for enrichment.\n///\n/// Each concrete implementation is a *hot-swappable* component that can be\n/// loaded from configuration at runtime.  We favour async traits in order to\n/// support network calls (language models, external toxicity APIs, \u2026).\n#[async_trait]\npub trait EnrichmentStrategy: Send + Sync {\n    async fn enrich(&self, event: EnrichedEvent) -> Result<EnrichedEvent, PipelineError>;\n\n    /// A short human-readable label used in metrics and logs.\n    fn name(&self) -> &'static str;\n}\n\n/// A quality control rule that inspects a value and returns success or failure.\npub trait DataQualityRule: Send + Sync {\n    fn check(&self, event: &SocialEvent) -> Result<(), PipelineError>;\n\n    /// Same semantic purpose as [`EnrichmentStrategy::name`].\n    fn name(&self) -> &'static str;\n}\n\n/// Validate that the text body is not empty or whitespace.\npub struct RuleNonEmptyText;\n\nimpl DataQualityRule for RuleNonEmptyText {\n    fn check(&self, event: &SocialEvent) -> Result<(), PipelineError> {\n        if event.text.trim().is_empty() {\n            Err(PipelineError::Validation(\n                \"Text payload must not be empty\".into(),\n            ))\n        } else {\n            Ok(())\n        }\n    }\n\n    fn name(&self) -> &'static str {\n        \"non_empty_text\"\n self.metrics\n                .latency\n                .with_label_values(&[\"pass\"])\n                .observe_duration(timer.stop_and_record());\n\n            let qe = QualifiedEvent {\n                original: event,\n                qc_passed: true,\n                failed_rule: None,\n            };\n            self.publish(&qe, &self.cfg.output_pass_topic).await?;\n            Ok(())\n  .payload(&payload)\n            .key(&qe.original.id);\n        let _ = self\n            .producer\n            .send(record, Duration::from_secs(0))\n            .await\n            .map_err(|(e,      info!(\"Received SIGINT, shutting down\");\n            }\n            _ = sig_term.recv() => {\n                info!(\"Received SIGTERM, shutting down\");\n            }\n        }\n     "content": "```rust\n//! module_27 \u2013 Enrichment Orchestrator\n//!\n//! This module implements the run-time pluggable enrichment pipeline that\n//! powers ChirpPulse\u2019s real-time social sentiment lake.  A registry of\n//! `EnrichmentStrategy`s can be (un)registered at run-time, enabling data\n//! scientists to hot-swap algorithms without redeploying micro-services.\n//!\n//! The orchestrator asynchronously consumes `SocialEvent`s from an upstream\n//! message queue (Kafka in production, but any `Stream<Item = SocialEvent>`\n//! will do), fans-out processing across registered strategies, merges the\n//! results, and publishes an `EnrichedEvent` downstream.\n//!\n//! Production-grade concerns addressed here:\n//!   \u2022 Cancellation safety & graceful shutdown (`shutdown` trigger)\n//!   \u2022 Back-pressure via a bounded channel\n//!   \u2022 Metrics / structured logging through `tracing`\n//!   \u2022 Robust error handling with typed errors\n//!   \u2022 Thread-safe shared registry powered by `DashMap`\n//!\n//! NOTE: Networking and external service calls (e.g. to a ML inference\n//!       cluster) are mocked for brevity.\n\nuse std::{\n    sync::Arc,\n    time::{Duration, SystemTime},\n};\n\nuse async_trait::async_trait;\nuse chrono::{DateTime, Utc};\nuse dashmap::DashMap;\nuse futures::{future::join_all, stream::StreamExt};\nuse serde::{Deserialize, Serialize};\nuse thiserror::Error;\nuse tokio::{\n    select,\n    sync::{broadcast, mpsc},\n    task::JoinHandle,\n    time::timeout,\n};\nuse tracing::{debug, error, info, instrument, warn};\n\n/// Maximum time a strategy may take before the orchestrator aborts it.\nconst STRATEGY_TIMEOUT: Duration = Duration::from_millis(800);\n\n/// Bounded size for the internal event queue.\nconst CHANNEL_DEPTH: usize = 1_024;\n\n/// Domain object representing a raw social event on the wire.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct SocialEvent {\n    pub id: String,\n    pub author: String,\n    pub text: String,\n    #[serde(with = \"ts_millis\")]\n    pub created_at: SystemTime,\n}\n\n/// Generic enrichment key/value.\npub type Enrichment = serde_json::Map<String, serde_json::Value>;\n\n/// Output object published downstream.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct EnrichedEvent {\n    pub source: SocialEvent,\n    pub enrichments: Enrichment,\n}\n\n/// Custom timestamp (de)serializer for millisecond precision.\nmod ts_millis {\n    use std::time::{Duration, SystemTime, UNIX_EPOCH};\n\n    use serde::{Deserialize, Deserializer, Serializer};\n\n    pub fn serialize<S>(ts: &SystemTime, s: S) -> Result<S::Ok, S::Error>\n    where\n        S: Serializer,\n    {\n        let millis = ts\n            .duration_since(UNIX_EPOCH)\n            .unwrap_or(Duration::ZERO)\n            .as_millis() as u64;\n        s.serialize_u64(millis)\n    }\n\n    pub fn deserialize<'de, D>(d: D) -> Result<SystemTime, D::Error>\n    where\n        D: Deserializer<'de>,\n    {\n        let ms = u64::deserialize(d)?;\n        Ok(UNIX_EPOCH + Duration::from_millis(ms))\n    }\n}\n\n/// Failure modes for individual strategies.\n#[derive(Debug, Error)]\npub enum StrategyError {\n    #[error(\"model inference failed: {0}\")]\n    Inference(String),\n\n    #[error(\"io error: {0}\")]\n    Io(#[from] std::io::Error),\n\n    #[error(\"timeout\")]\n    Timeout,\n\n    #[error(\"unknown: {0}\")]\n    Other(String),\n}\n\n/// Failure modes for the orchestrator itself.\n#[derive(Debug, Error)]\npub enum OrchestratorError {\n    #[error(transparent)]\n    Strategy(#[from] StrategyError),\n\n    #[error(\"channel closed\")]\n    ChannelClosed,\n\n    #[error(\"shutdown requested\")]\n    Shutdown,\n\n    #[error(\"task join error: {0}\")]\n    Join(#[from] tokio::task::JoinError),\n}\n\n/// Runtime pluggable enrichment strategy.\n///\n/// Implementations are required to be `Send + Sync` so they may be shared\n/// across tokio worker threads.  A real implementation might call out to a\n/// TensorFlow serving cluster, make an HTTP request, or reference an on-disk\n/// model; here we use a toy implementation for illustration.\n#[async_trait]\npub trait EnrichmentStrategy: Send + Sync + 'static {\n    /// Human-readable identifier for logging & registry keys.\n    fn name(&self) -> &'static str;\n\n    /// Attempts to enrich the event, returning a partial `Enrichment`.\n    ///\n    /// The orchestrator will merge the individual strategy outputs into a\n    /// single document.  Returning `Ok(None)` indicates that the strategy\n    /// deliberately produced no output (e.g. unsupported language).\n    async fn enrich(&self, event: &SocialEvent) -> Result<Option<Enrichment>, StrategyError>;\n}\n\n/// Thread-safe registry for run-time strategy hot-swapping.\n#[derive(Debug, Default)]\npub struct StrategyRegistry {\n    strategies: DashMap<String, Arc<dyn EnrichmentStrategy>>,\n}\n\nimpl StrategyRegistry {\n    pub fn new() -> Self {\n        Self::default()\n    }\n\n    /// Registers or replaces a strategy.\n    pub fn register<S>(&self, strategy: S)\n    where\n        S: EnrichmentStrategy,\n    {\n        let key = strategy.name().to_lowercase();\n        self.strategies.insert(key, Arc::new(strategy));\n        info!(strategy = %key, \"strategy registered\");\n    }\n\n    /// Removes a strategy from the registry.\n    pub fn unregister(&self, name: &str) {\n        self.strategies.remove(name);\n        info!(strategy = %name, \"strategy unregistered\");\n    }\n\n    /// Snapshot of the current strategies.\n    pub fn snapshot(&self) -> Vec<Arc<dyn EnrichmentStrategy>> {\n        self.strategies.iter().map(|s| Arc::clone(s.value())).collect()\n    }\n}\n\n/// Orchestrates ingestion, fan-out enrichment, and publication.\npub struct EnrichmentOrchestrator {\n    input_rx: mpsc::Receiver<SocialEvent>,\n    output_tx: mpsc::Sender<EnrichedEvent>,\n    registry: StrategyRegistry,\n    shutdown_rx: broadcast::Receiver<()>,\n}\n\n/// Builder for `EnrichmentOrchestrator`.\npub struct OrchestratorBuilder {\n    registry: StrategyRegistry,\n    shutdown_rx: broadcast::Receiver<()>,\n}\n\nimpl OrchestratorBuilder {\n    pub fn new(shutdown_rx: broadcast::Receiver<()>) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            registry: StrategyRegistry::new(),\n            shutdown_rx,\n        }\n    }\n\n    pub fn with_strategy<S>(mut self, strategy: S) -> Self\n    where\n        S: EnrichmentStrategy,\n    {\n        self.registry.register(strategy);\n        self\n    }\n\n    pub fn build(\n        self,\n    ) -> (\n        EnrichmentOrchestrator,\n        mpsc::Sender<SocialEvent>,\n        mpsc::Receiver<EnrichedEvent>,\n    ) {\n        let (in_tx, in_rx) = mpsc::channel(CHANNEL_DEPTH);\n        let (out_tx, out_rx) = mpsc::channel(CHANNEL_DEPTH);\n        (\n            EnrichmentOrchestrator {\n                input_rx: in_rx,\n                output_tx: out_tx,\n                registry: self.registry,\n                shutdown_rx: self.shutdown_rx,\n            },\n            in_tx,\n            out_rx,\n        )\n    }\n}\n\nimpl EnrichmentOrchestrator {\n    /// Starts the main processing loop.  Returns when shutdown is requested\n    /// or an unrecoverable error occurs.\n    #[instrument(skip(self))]\n    pub async fn run(mut self) -> Result<(), OrchestratorError> {\n        loop {\n            select! {\n                _ = self.shutdown_rx.recv() => {\n                    info!(\"shutdown signal received\");\n                    return Err(OrchestratorError::Shutdown);\n                }\n                maybe_event = self.input_rx.recv() => {\n                    let event = maybe_event.ok_or(OrchestratorError::ChannelClosed)?;\n                    debug!(event_id = %event.id, \"received event\");\n                    let record = self.handle_event(event).await?;\n                    self.output_tx\n                        .send(record)\n                        .await\n                        .map_err(|_| OrchestratorError::ChannelClosed)?;\n                }\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    #[instrument(skip(self, event))]\n    async fn handle_event(&self, event: SocialEvent) -> Result<EnrichedEvent, OrchestratorError> {\n        let strategies = self.registry.snapshot();\n        let mut tasks: Vec<JoinHandle<_>> = Vec::with_capacity(strategies.len());\n\n        for strat in strategies {\n            let e = event.clone();\n            tasks.push(tokio::spawn(async move {\n                let name = strat.name();\n                let result = timeout(STRATEGY_TIMEOUT, strat.enrich(&e)).await;\n                match result {\n                    Ok(Ok(enrichment)) => Ok((name, enrichment)),\n                    Ok(Err(e)) => Err((name, StrategyError::from(e))),\n                    Err(_) => Err((name, StrategyError::Timeout)),\n                }\n            }));\n        }\n\n        let mut merged = Enrichment::new();\n\n        for handle in tasks {\n            match handle.await? {\n                Ok((name, Some(partial))) => {\n                    debug!(strategy = %name, \"enrichment succeeded\");\n                    merged.extend(partial);\n                }\n                Ok((name, None)) => {\n                    debug!(strategy = %name, \"no enrichment produced\");\n                }\n                Err((name, err)) => {\n                    warn!(strategy = %name, %err, \"enrichment failed\");\n                    // Continue processing; per-strategy failures are tolerated.\n                }\n            }\n        }\n\n        Ok(EnrichedEvent {\n            source: event,\n            enrichments: merged,\n        })\n    }\n}\n\n/* ------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n/* Built-in demo strategies                                                  */\n/* serde_json::json!(score));\n        Ok(Some(map))\n    }\n}\n\n/// Toy language detector based on the presence of unicode ranges.\npub struct SimpleLangDetect;\n\n#[async_trait]\nimpl fn version(&self) -> &str;\n\n    /// Perform the analysis.  Must be fast (<1 ms) or spawn its own blocking task.\n    async fn score(&self, text: &str) -> Result<f32>;\n}\n\n/// Extremely naive, rule-based heuristic sentiment scorer.\n/// Suitable as a safe-mode fallback when heavy ML models fail.\npub struct RuleBasedStrategy;\n\n#[async_trait]\nimpl SentimentStrategy for RuleBasedStrategy {\n    fn version(&self) -> &str {\n        \"rule-based-v1\"\n    }\n\n    async fn score(&self, text: &str) -> Result<f32> {\n        let lowered = text.to_ascii_lowercase();\n        let pos = [\"good\", \"love\", \"awesome\", \"yay\"]\n            .iter()\n            .filter(|w| lowered.contains(*w))\n            .count() as f32;\n        let neg = [\"bad\", \"hate\", \"terrible\", \"boo\"]\n            .iter()\n            .filter(|w| lowered.contains(*w))\n            .count() as f32;\n\n        Ok(match (pos - neg).clamp(-5.0, 5.0) {\n            x if x > 0.0 => x / 5.0,\n            x if x < 0.0 => x / 5.0,\n            _ => 0.0,\n        })\n    }\n}\n\n/// Placeholder for an ML-based implementation.  Here we fake the latency but\n/// the interface would realistically make a gRPC/tch-rs/onnxruntime call.\npub struct MlStrategy;\n\n#[async_trait]\nimpl SentimentStrategy for MlStrategy {\n    fn version(&self) -> &str {\n        \"ml-bert-v3\"\n    }\n\n    async fn score(&self, text: &str) -> Result<f32> {\n        // Simulate inferencing latency\n        tokio::time::sleep(Duration::from_millis(2)).await;\n        // For brevity: randomish score based on hash\n        let hash = seahash::hash(text.as_bytes());\n        Ok((hash % 2000) as f32 / 1000.0 - 1.0) // Value in [-1.0, 1.0]\n    }\n}\n\n// --------------- Config & Hot-Reloading ---------------------------\n\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Deserialize)]\n#[serde(rename_all = \"snake_case\")]\nenum StrategyKind {\n    RuleBased,\n    Ml,\n}\n\nimpl StrategyKind {\n    fn build(self) -> Arc<dyn SentimentStrategy> {\n        match self {\n            StrategyKind::RuleBased => Arc::new(RuleBasedStrategy),\n            StrategyKind::Ml => Arc::new(MlStrategy),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Deserialize)]\npub struct EngineConfig {\n    /// Which strategy to use for scoring\n    strategy: StrategyKind,\n\n    /// How many enrichment worker tasks to spawn\n    #[serde(default = \"EngineConfig::default_parallelism\")]\n    parallelism: usize,\n}\n\nimpl EngineConfig {\n    fn default_parallelism() -> usize {\n        num_cpus::get().max(2)\n    }\n}\n\nimpl Default for EngineConfig {\n    fn default() -> Self {\n        Self {\n            strategy: StrategyKind::RuleBased,\n            parallelism: Self::default_parallelism(),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\nasync fn load_config(path: &Path) -> Result<EngineConfig> {\n    let data = fs::read_to_string(path)\n        .await\n        .with_context(|| format!(\"reading config file {}\", path.display()))?;\n    let cfg: EngineConfig =\n        toml::from_str(&data).with_context(|| \"parsing engine config TOML\")?;\n    Ok(cfg)\n}\n\n// --------------- Sentiment Engine --------------------------------\n\npub struct SentimentEngine {\n    /// Sender for raw events\n    pub in_tx: mpsc::Sender<api::RawEvent>,\n    /// Receiver for enriched events\n    pub out_rx: mpsc::Receiver<api::EnrichedEvent>,\n    /// Handle to shutdown signal\n    shutdown_tx: watch::Sender<bool>,\n}\n",

Sentiment Analysis Stage (CPU-Intensive)\n\n```rust\n// File: /app/project/src/module_27.txt\n// Lines: 302-327 (Naive sentiment strategy - CPU intensive)\npub struct NaiveSentiment;\n\n#[async_trait]\nimpl EnrichmentStrategy for NaiveSentiment {\n    fn name(&self) -> &'static str {\n        \"naive_sentiment\"\n    }\n\n    async fn enrich(&self, event: &SocialEvent) -> Result<Option<Enrichment>, StrategyError> {\n        // Simulate heavy computation.\n        tokio::time::sleep(Duration::from_millis(50)).await;\n\n        let score = if event.text.contains(\"love\") {\n            1.0\n        } else if event.text.contains(\"hate\") {\n            -1.0\n        } else {\n            0.0\n        };\n\n        let mut map = Enrichment::new();\n        map.insert(\"sentiment_score\".into(), serde_json::json!(score));\n        Ok(Some(map))\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### 4. Back-pressure Mechanism in Current Architecture\n\n```rust\n// File: /app/project/src/module_78.txt\n// Lines: 362-365 (Back-pressure when channel is full)\n                    Ok(enriched) => {\n                        let latency = SystemTime::now().duration_since(started).unwrap_or_default();\n                        histogram!(\"pipeline.event.latency_ms\", latency.as_millis() as f64);\n                        if let Err(err) = output.send(enriched).await {\n                            error!(error=%err, \"failed to forward enriched event\");\n                            return Err(PipelineError::ChannelClosed);\n                        }\n                    }\n```\n\n### 5. Current Kafka Configuration\n\n```toml\n# File: /app/project/src/config.txt\n# Lines: 60-77 (Pipeline configuration showing worker pool sizes)\n[[pipelines]]\nname               = \"language_detection\"\nenabled            = true\ninput_topic        = \"social_raw\"\noutput_topic       = \"social_lang\"\nworker_pool_size   = 16\ntimeout_ms         = 3_000\nstrategy_impl      = \"lang_detect::FastTextStrategy\"\n\n[[pipelines]]\nname               = \"toxicity_scoring\"\nenabled            = true\ninput_topic        = \"social_lang\"\noutput_topic       = \"social_toxic\"\nworker_pool_size   = 24\ntimeout_ms         = 5_000\ndependencies       = [\"language_detection\"]\nstrategy_impl      = \"toxicity::PerspectiveStrategy\"\n```\n\n## Analysis\n\n### 1. Pipeline Mapping (4 Primary Stages)\n\nThe ChirpPulse data processing pipeline consists of the following stages:\n\n| Stage | Purpose | Key Module(s) |\n|-------|---------|---------------|\n| **1. Ingestion** | Consumes raw social events from external sources (Twitter, Reddit, Discord) via Kafka | module_12, module_47, module_70 |\n| **2. Data Normalization/Quality Control** | Schema validation, deduplication, PII removal, language detection | module_79, module_29, module_41, module_30 |\n| **3. Sentiment Analysis/Enrichment** | CPU-intensive sentiment scoring, toxicity detection, graph extraction | module_22, module_27, module_56, module_10 |\n| **4. Storage Sink** | Writes enriched data to Apache Iceberg tables on S3 | module_65, Kafka producer to `chirp.enriched.events` |\n\n### 2. Bottleneck Analysis: The tokio::sync::mpsc Channel Coupling\n\n**Identified Mechanism:** The coupling between the normalization stage and sentiment analysis stage occurs via `tokio::sync::mpsc::channel` with a bounded capacity.\n\n**Critical Code Location:** `/app/project/src/module_27.txt` lines 216-217\n\n```rust\nconst CHANNEL_DEPTH: usize = 1_024;\n// ...\nlet (in_tx, in_rx) = mpsc::channel(CHANNEL_DEPTH);\nlet (out_tx, out_rx) = mpsc::channel(CHANNEL_DEPTH);\n```\n\n**How This Causes Backpressure:**\n\n1. **Bounded Buffer Exhaustion**: The `mpsc::channel(1_024)` creates a bounded channel with capacity for only 1,024 events. When the sentiment analysis stage (consumer) processes events slower than the normalization stage (producer) produces them, the buffer fills up.\n\n2. **Blocking Send Behavior**: When the channel is full, `output.send(enriched).await` blocks the producer task, causing backpressure to propagate upstream to the normalization stage.\n\n3. **Single-Process Coupling**: Both producer and consumer run in the same process. If the sentiment analysis stage becomes overloaded (e.g., ML model inference latency spikes), it directly impacts the normalization stage's throughput.\n\n4. **No Durability**: In-memory mpsc channels provide no persistence. If the process crashes while the channel contains events, those events are lost.\n\n5. **Vertical Scaling Limitation**: The consumer and producer cannot be scaled independently - they are coupled in the same deployment unit.\n\n**With the FireHose Integration**: The new high-throughput source will produce events at a rate far exceeding the sentiment analysis stage's capacity. The bounded channel (1,024 events) will fill within milliseconds, causing:\n- Upstream stalling (normalization stops accepting new events)\n- Potential memory pressure from buffered events\n- Risk of data loss during process restarts\n\n### 3. Proposed Architectural Solution: External Message Queue Decoupling\n\n**Pattern: Asynchronous Message Queue / Event-Driven Architecture**\n\nReplace the in-process `tokio::sync::mpsc` channel with an external, durable message queue (Apache Kafka) to decouple the normalization and sentiment analysis stages.\n\n**Proposed Architecture:**\n\n```\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510      \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510      \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502   Ingestion     \u2502      \u2502   Normalization  \u2502      \u2502    Sentiment      \u2502\n\u2502   Gateway       \u2502 \u2500\u2500\u25b6  \u2502   Service        \u2502 \u2500\u2500\u25b6  \u2502    Service        \u2502\n\u2502 (multiple pods) \u2502 \u2502                        Apache Kafka Cluster                       \u2502\n \u2502  \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510  \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510  \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510  \u2502\n \u2502  \u2502 raw.events     \u2502  \u2502 normalized.events   \u2502  \u2502 enriched      \u2502  \u2502\n \u2502  \u2502 (partitioned)  \u2502  \u2502 (partitioned)       \u2502  \u2502 .events       \u2502  \u2502\n \u2502  \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518 \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518  \u2502\n Changes:**\n\n1. **Introduce `chirp.normalized.events` Kafka Topic**: Create a new intermediate Kafka topic between normalization and sentiment analysis.\n\n2. **Normalization Service as Kafka Producer**: After normalizing events, publish to `chirp.normalized.events` instead of an in-process channel.\n\n3. **Sentiment Service as Independent Kafka Consumer**: Run sentiment analysis as a separate microservice that consumes from `chirp.normalized.events` and produces to `chirp.enriched.events`.\n\n4. **Consumer Group Scaling**: The sentiment service can scale horizontally via Kafka consumer groups, with each consumer handling a subset of partitions.\n\n### 4. Justification of Proposed Solution\n\n| Benefit | Explanation |\n|---------|-------------|\n| **Scalability** | Sentiment analysis can scale independently by adding more consumer instances. Kafka partitions enable parallel processing across multiple pods. |\n| **Resilience** | Kafka provides message durability. If the sentiment service crashes, messages persist and can be reprocessed. No data loss during deployments or failures. |\n| **Backpressure Handling** | Kafka acts as an elastic buffer. The normalization stage continues producing at full speed while the sentiment stage processes at its own pace. Lag is absorbed by Kafka's disk-backed storage. |\n| **Decoupled Deployment** | Each stage can be deployed, updated, and scaled independently without affecting others. |\n| **Observability** | Consumer lag metrics from Kafka provide visibility into processing throughput and bottlenecks. |\n| **Exactly-Once Semantics** | Kafka's transactional semantics (already configured in config.txt: `enable_idempotence = true`) ensure no duplicate processing. |\n\n**Why This Pattern Over Alternatives:**\n\n- **vs. Increasing channel buffer**: Does not address fundamental scalability limits; still single-process.\n- **vs. Adding more worker threads**: Limited by single-machine resources; sentiment analysis is CPU/GPU bound.\n- **vs. Batch processing**: Loses real-time latency requirements stated in the README.\n\n### 5. Affected Components and Required Modifications\n\n| Module | File | Required Changes |\n|--------|------|------------------|\n| **module_27** | /app/project/src/module_27.txt | Replace `mpsc::channel` with Kafka producer. Change `build()` to return a Kafka topic name instead of `mpsc::Sender`. Modify `run()` loop to produce to Kafka instead of channel. |\n| **module_22** | /app/project/src/module_22.txt | Already uses Kafka. Update `INPUT_TOPIC` constant to consume from the new intermediate topic `chirp.normalized.events`. Ensure consumer group configuration supports horizontal scaling. |\n| **module_56** | /app/project/src/module_56.txt | Replace `mpsc::Receiver<api::RawEvent>` with Kafka consumer. Modify `SentimentEngine::new()` to create a Kafka consumer instead of receiving an mpsc channel. |\n| **module_79** | /app/project/src/module_79.txt | Update `SINK_TOPIC` to point to the new intermediate topic. Ensure producer is configured for high throughput. |\n| **config.txt** | /app/project/src/config.txt | Add new `[[pipelines]]` entry for the intermediate topic. Configure partition count for the new topic (recommend: equal to expected peak throughput / sentiment throughput per partition). Add new Kafka topic to `kafka_topics` section. |\n| **constants.txt** | /app/project/src/constants.txt | Add `pub const NORMALIZED_EVENTS: &str = \"chirp.normalized.events\";` to the `kafka_topics` module. |\n\n**Specific Code Changes for module_27:**\n\n```rust\n// BEFORE (module_27.txt, lines 216-217):\nlet (in_tx, in_rx) = mpsc::channel(CHANNEL_DEPTH);\nlet (out_tx, out_rx) = mpsc::channel(CHANNEL_DEPTH);\n\n// AFTER:\n// Remove in-process channels entirely.\n// Normalization publishes directly to Kafka topic.\n// Sentiment service consumes from Kafka topic in separate process.\n```\n\n**Specific Config Changes for config.txt:**\n\n```toml\n# Add new intermediate topic configuration\n[[pipelines]]\nname               = \"normalization_output\"\nenabled            = true\ninput_topic        = \"social_qc_valid\"\noutput_topic       = \"social_normalized\"  # NEW INTERMEDIATE TOPIC\nworker_pool_size   = 16\ntimeout_ms         = 2_000\n\n[[pipelines]]\nname               = \"sentiment_analysis\"\nenabled            = true\ninput_topic        = \"social_normalized\"  # CONSUME FROM NEW TOPIC\noutput_topic       = \"social_enriched\"\nworker_pool_size   = 32  # Can be increased independently\ntimeout_ms         = 10_000\nauto_scale         = true  # Enable Kubernetes HPA\n```\n\n## Summary\n\n- **Primary finding**: The bottleneck between normalization and sentiment analysis is caused by a bounded `tokio::sync::mpsc::channel(1_024)` in module_27, which creates tight coupling and backpressure when the sentiment stage cannot keep pace with incoming events.\n\n- **Key components**:\n  - module_27 (Enrichment Orchestrator) - contains the critical mpsc channel coupling\n  - module_22 (Sentiment Stream Processor) - the slow consumer\n  - module_79 (QC Pipeline) - upstream producer\n  - config.txt - pipeline configuration\n\n- **Architectural pattern**: **Message Queue Decoupling** using Apache Kafka as an intermediate buffer between stages, enabling independent horizontal scaling and providing durability.\n\n- **Recommendations**:\n  1. Introduce `chirp.normalized.events` Kafka topic as intermediate buffer\n  2. Convert module_27's orchestrator to a Kafka producer\n  3. Deploy sentiment analysis (module_22/module_56) as independent auto-scaled consumers\n  4. Configure Kafka topic with sufficient partitions (8-16) for parallelism\n  5. Implement consumer lag alerting to monitor backlog growth\n",

\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510  \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510  \u2502\n \u2502  \u2502 raw.events     \u2502  \u2502 normalized.events   \u2502  \u2502 enriched      \u2502  \u2502\n \u2502  \u2502 (partitioned)  \u2502  \u2502 (partitioned)       \u2502  \u2502 .events       \u2502  \u2502\n \u2502  \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518  \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518  \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518  \u2502\n \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n```\n\n**Key Changes:**\n\n1. **Introduce `chirp.normalized.events` Kafka Topic**: Create a new intermediate Kafka topic between normalization and sentiment analysis.\n\n2. **Normalization Service as Kafka Producer**: After normalizing events, publish to `chirp.normalized.events` instead of an in-process channel.\n\n3. **Sentiment Service as Independent Kafka Consumer**: Run sentiment analysis as a separate microservice that consumes from `chirp.normalized.events` and produces to `chirp.enriched.events`.\n\n4. **Consumer Group Scaling**: The sentiment service can scale horizontally via Kafka consumer groups, with each consumer handling a subset of partitions.\n\n### 4. Justification of Proposed Solution\n\n| Benefit | Explanation |\n|---------|-------------|\n| **Scalability** | Sentiment analysis can scale independently by adding more consumer instances. Kafka partitions enable parallel processing across multiple pods. |\n| **Resilience** | Kafka provides message durability. If the sentiment service crashes, messages persist and can be reprocessed. No data loss during deployments or failures. |\n| **Backpressure Handling** | Kafka acts as an elastic buffer. The normalization stage continues producing at full speed while the sentiment stage processes at its own pace. Lag is absorbed by Kafka's disk-backed storage. |\n| **Decoupled Deployment** | Each stage can be deployed, updated, and scaled independently without affecting others. |\n| **Observability** | Consumer lag metrics from Kafka provide visibility into processing throughput and bottlenecks. |\n| **Exactly-Once Semantics** | Kafka's transactional semantics (already configured in config.txt: `enable_idempotence = true`) ensure no duplicate processing. |\n\n**Why This Pattern Over Alternatives:**\n\n- **vs. Increasing channel buffer**: Does not address fundamental scalability limits; still single-process.\n- **vs. Adding more worker threads**: Limited by single-machine resources; sentiment analysis is CPU/GPU bound.\n- **vs. Batch processing**: Loses real-time latency requirements stated in the README.\n\n### 5. Affected Components and Required Modifications\n\n| Module | File | Required Changes |\n|--------|------|------------------|\n| **module_27** | /app/project/src/module_27.txt | Replace `mpsc::channel` with Kafka producer. Change `build()` to return a Kafka topic name instead of `mpsc::Sender`. Modify `run()` loop to produce to Kafka instead of channel. |\n| **module_22** | /app/project/src/module_22.txt | Already uses Kafka. Update `INPUT_TOPIC` constant to consume from the new intermediate topic `chirp.normalized.events`. Ensure consumer group configuration supports horizontal scaling. |\n| **module_56** | /app/project/src/module_56.txt | Replace `mpsc::Receiver<api::RawEvent>` with Kafka consumer. Modify `SentimentEngine::new()` to create a Kafka consumer instead of receiving an mpsc channel. |\n| **module_79** | /app/project/src/module_79.txt | Update `SINK_TOPIC` to point to the new intermediate topic. Ensure producer is configured for high throughput. |\n| **config.txt** | /app/project/src/config.txt | Add new `[[pipelines]]` entry for the intermediate topic. Configure partition count for the new topic (recommend: equal to expected peak throughput / sentiment throughput per partition). Add new Kafka topic to `kafka_topics` section. |\n| **constants.txt** | /app/project/src/constants.txt | Add `pub const NORMALIZED_EVENTS: &str = \"chirp.normalized.events\";` to the `kafka_topics` module. |\n\n**Specific Code Changes for module_27:**\n\n```rust\n// BEFORE (module_27.txt, lines 216-217):\nlet (in_tx, in_rx) = mpsc::channel(CHANNEL_DEPTH);\nlet (out_tx, out_rx) = mpsc::channel(CHANNEL_DEPTH);\n\n// AFTER:\n// Remove in-process channels entirely.\n// Normalization publishes directly to Kafka topic.\n// Sentiment service consumes from Kafka topic in separate process.\n```\n\n**Specific Config Changes for config.txt:**\n\n```toml\n# Add new intermediate topic configuration\n[[pipelines]]\nname               = \"normalization_output\"\nenabled            = true\ninput_topic        = \"social_qc_valid\"\noutput_topic       = \"social_normalized\"  # NEW INTERMEDIATE TOPIC\nworker_pool_size   = 16\ntimeout_ms         = 2_000\n\n[[pipelines]]\nname               = \"sentiment_analysis\"\nenabled            = true\ninput_topic        = \"social_normalized\"  # CONSUME FROM NEW TOPIC\noutput_topic       = \"social_enriched\"\nworker_pool_size   = 32  # Can be increased independently\ntimeout_ms         = 10_000\nauto_scale         = true  # Enable Kubernetes HPA\n```\n\n## Summary\n\n- **Primary finding**: The bottleneck between normalization and sentiment analysis is caused by a bounded `tokio::sync::mpsc::channel(1_024)` in module_27, which creates tight coupling and backpressure when the sentiment stage cannot keep pace with incoming events.\n\n- **Key components**:\n  - module_27 (Enrichment Orchestrator) - contains the critical mpsc channel coupling\n  - module_22 (Sentiment Stream Processor) - the slow consumer\n  - module_79 (QC Pipeline) - upstream producer\n  - config.txt - pipeline configuration\n\n- **Architectural pattern**: **Message Queue Decoupling** using Apache Kafka as an intermediate buffer between stages, enabling independent horizontal scaling and providing durability.\n\n- **Recommendations**:\n  1. Introduce `chirp.normalized.events` Kafka topic as intermediate buffer\n  2. Convert module_27's orchestrator to a Kafka producer\n  3. Deploy sentiment analysis (module_22/module_56) as independent auto-scaled consumers\n  4. Configure Kafka topic with sufficient partitions (8-16) for parallelism\n  5. Implement consumer lag alerting to monitor backlog growth\n",

# Solution: rust_data_streaming_expert_013_architectural_understanding_expert_01

## Key Files Identified

### Core Pipeline Orchestration
- /app/project/src/module_27.txt - **Enrichment Orchestrator**: The critical module that connects normalization to sentiment analysis via bounded mpsc channels (CHANNEL_DEPTH = 1,024)
- /app/project/src/module_22.txt - **Sentiment Analysis Processor**: Hot-swappable sentiment strategy implementation with Kafka stream processing
- /app/project/src/module_79.txt - **Quality Control Pipeline**: QC/Enrich micro-service that validates and enriches events after raw ingestion

### Data Normalization/Transformation
- /app/project/src/module_78.txt - **Enrichment Pipeline**: Real-time enrichment with data-quality checks, strategy pattern implementation
- /app/project/src/module_47.txt - **Dynamic Pipeline Runner**: Self-healing streaming pipeline with configurable stages

### Sentiment Analysis
- /app/project/src/module_56.txt - **Sentiment Engine**: Reconfigurable sentiment scoring with hot-swap capability (CHANNEL_CAPACITY = 16,384)
- /app/project/src/module_10.txt - **Dynamic Enrichment Pipeline**: Pluggable enrichment stages including ToxicityScorer

### Data Quality
- /app/project/src/module_29.txt - **Data Quality Engine**: Stream validator with configurable checks
- /app/project/src/module_41.txt - **Data Quality Enforcement Micro-service**: QC rules and Kafka integration
- /app/project/src/module_30.txt - **Quality Gate**: Pluggable validation engine

### Configuration
- /app/project/src/config.txt - **Global Runtime Configuration**: TOML config with pipeline settings, worker pool sizes, queue depths
- /app/project/src/constants.txt - **Centralized Constants**: Kafka topics, batch sizes, retry policies
